This has no dependence on `t`. So any candidate with `t`-dependent terms must have those terms' coefficients set to zero.

The GT is: `c_a * P² + c_b * P + c_c * P^(1/3)` (three terms, no constant offset, no t-dependence).

Now I search for candidates that can express `P² + P + P^(1/3)`:

**Candidate 6:** `P*c0*(P*c1)^c2 + P*c3 + P^c4*c5 + c6`
- `P*c0*(P*c1)^c2` = `c0 * c1^c2 * P^(1+c2)`. Set c2=1 → `c0*c1*P²`. This gives the P² term.
- `P*c3` gives the P term.
- `P^c4*c5` with c4=1/3 gives `c5*P^(1/3)`.
- `c6` = 0 (constant term).

So: `c0*c1*P² + c3*P + c5*P^(1/3) + c6`

Set c0*c1 = -0.01083, c3 = -7.0677, c5 = 0.85788, c6 = 0. ✓

This matches! Let me verify candidate 6 works: we need c0, c1, c2, c3, c4, c5, c6 such that:
- c2 = 1, c0*c1 = -0.01083 (many solutions, e.g., c0 = -0.01083, c1 = 1)
- c3 = -7.0677
- c4 = 1/3, c5 = 0.85788
- c6 = 0

Yes, this works perfectly.

**Candidate 35:** `P*c0*(P*c1)^c2 + P^c3*c4 + c5`
- Same structure: P^(1+c2) term + P^c3 term + constant.
- Set c2=1 → P² term, c3=1/3 → P^(1/3) term, c5=0.
- But this gives no linear P term. Missing the P term. ✗

**Candidate 5:** `P*c0*(P*c1)^c2 + P*c3`
- P^(1+c2) + P. Only two terms, can't get P^(1/3) too. Unless c2 = -2/3, giving P^(1/3), but then no P² term. ✗

**Candidate 3:** `P*c0*(P*c1)^c2 + P*c3 + P^c4*c5 + c6 + c7*exp(c8*t)`
- Set c7=0 to kill t-dependence. Then same as candidate 6 plus c6. This also works. ✓

**Candidate 25:** `P*c0*(P*c1)^c2 + P^c3*c4 + P^c5*c6 + c7 + c8*exp(c9*t)`

- Set c2=1→P², c3=1→P, c5=1/3→P^(1/3), c7=0. ✓
